## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P (and possibly explicit time dependence t). This is a classic population-dynamics setting where mechanistic models express per-capita growth, density dependence, and time-varying forcing via ODE structures.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant-rate growth: dP_dt = c0 (linear increase independent of P; e.g., constant stocking/harvest net effect)
- Affine per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * P) * P (linear density dependence in per-capita growth)
- Logistic (Verhulst) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying-capacity-like limitation with K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (flexible density dependence curvature)
- Gompertz ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic density dependence; asymmetric approach to saturation)
- Richards generalized logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) * (c1 * P) ** c3 (adds shape control beyond theta-logistic)
- Allee effect (strong) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P; extinction threshold near P = 1/c2)
- Allee effect (smooth rational) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P / (P + c2)) (weak Allee-like low-density suppression without a hard threshold)
- Harvesting (linear) with density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita removal/harvest proportional to P)
- Harvesting (constant yield) with density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removals; can induce collapse at low P)
- Time-varying growth rate (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (changing environment or management over time)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental forcing on per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (environmental capacity): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t))) (capacity fluctuates seasonally)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth g(P) inferred via structure dP_dt = P * g(P): multiplicative P indicates births/deaths proportional to population size.
- Negative density dependence shows up as decreasing g(P) with P (e.g., g(P)=c0-c1*P or g(P)=c0*log(c1/P)), producing slowing growth as P increases.
- A finite carrying capacity is suggested by a factor that changes sign at some P (e.g., (1 - c1*P) or (1 - (c1*P)**c2)), implying dP_dtŌēł0 at equilibrium.
- Asymmetric approach to equilibrium (rapid early growth, slow late growth) often aligns with Gompertz-type log(c/P) rather than quadratic logistic inhibition.
- Depressed growth at small P (Allee effect) is indicated by an extra low-density suppression factor such as (c2*P-1) or P/(P+c2), potentially creating a critical threshold.
- External removals/harvest are indicated by subtractive terms not multiplied by (1 - c1*P), e.g., -c2*P (proportional harvest) or -c2 (constant yield).
- Environmental change over time appears as explicit t-dependence in coefficients (c0+c1*t) or periodic modulation (sin(c*t+c)), even if density dependence remains present.
- Equilibria multiplicity can be diagnosed by polynomial factors in P (e.g., P*(1-c1*P)*(c2*P-1)), implying multiple fixed points and possible bistability.

\[

Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.7013915187P-\frac{0.7013915187}{65.7541311409}P^2
\]
So GT has exactly three terms: \( (\text{const})\cdot P\sin(\omega t)\), \( (\text{const})\cdot P\), \( (\text{const})\cdot P^2\), and **no** other dependence (no constant offset, no logs/exp, no extra sinusoids, no \(1/t^2\), etc.).

Let
- \(A=0.8770002846\)
- \(\omega=0.5671736066\)
- \(B=0.7013915187\)
- \(D=-B/65.7541311409\) (the \(P^2\) coefficient)

A candidate matches iff it can be reduced (by choosing its constants) to:
\[
D\,P^2 + B\,P + A\,P\sin(\omega t)
\]

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4)\)
Set \(c0=D,\; c1=B,\; c2=A,\; c3=\omega,\; c4=0\). Then it equals GT. **Matches.**

### 2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + Pc5\)
Combine linear terms: \(P(c1+c5)\). Set \(c0=D,\; c2=A,\; c4=\omega,\; c3=0,\; c1+c5=B\). **Matches.**

### 3. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4}c5\)
To match GTŌĆÖs \(P^2\) term, need \(c4=2,\; c5=D\). Then set \(c1=A,\; c2=\omega,\; c3=0,\; c0=B\). **Matches.**

### 4. \(Pc0\sin(c1 t + c2) + Pc3/t^2 + P + P^{c4}c5 + c6 + c7e^{Pc8}\)
Extra terms \(P/t^2\), constant \(c6\), and exponential cannot be present in GT for all \(t,P\). You can set \(c3=0,\; c6=0,\; c7=0\). Then you still have a forced \(+P\) term, but GTŌĆÖs linear coefficient is \(B\neq 1\); you can absorb by setting \(P^{c4}c5\) to contribute additional linear term only if \(c4=1\), but then you lose \(P^2\). If \(c4=2\) to get \(P^2\), you canŌĆÖt adjust the linear coefficient away from 1 except via \(Pc0\sin(\cdot)\) which is not linear-in-\(P\) alone. **No match.**

### 5. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + c4\log(Pc5+1)+c6+c7\sin(c8 t+c9)\)
Set log term off: \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) with \(c4=0\) anyway), set \(c6=0\), set extra sine off \(c7=0\). Left with \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot)+P\). Same issue: linear coefficient forced to 1, but GTŌĆÖs is \(B\neq 1\). **No match.**

### 6. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + c4 t/(Pc5+c6)+ c7/(Pc5+c6)+c8\)
Turn off rational terms: \(c4=0,\; c7=0\). Set \(c8=0\). Left with \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot)+P\) ŌåÆ linear coefficient forced 1. **No match.**

### 7. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + c4\log(Pc5+1)+c6\)
Set \(c4=0,\; c6=0\). Left with \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot)+P\) ŌåÆ linear coefficient forced 1. **No match.**

### 8. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + Pc4 + c5\)
Set \(c5=0\). Choose \(c0=D,\; c1=A,\; c2=\omega,\; c3=0,\; c4=B\). **Matches.**

### 9. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + Pc4 + P + c5\)
Even with \(c5=0\), linear term is \(P(c4+1)\). That can equal \(BP\) by setting \(c4=B-1\). Then set \(c0=D,\; c1=A,\; c2=\omega,\; c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 10. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + Pc4/(Pc5+c6) + P + c7/(Pc5+c6)+c8\)
To avoid non-polynomial dependence on \(P\), must set \(c4=0,\; c7=0\). Then reduce to \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot)+P+c8\). Need \(c8=0\), but still linear coefficient forced 1. **No match.**

### 11. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + c4e^{Pc5}+c6\)
Set \(c4=0,\; c6=0\). Left with forced \(+P\). **No match.**

### 12. Same as 11 plus extra sine
Set \(c4=0,\; c6=0,\; c7=0\). Still forced \(+P\). **No match.**

### 13. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + Pc4(c5+t)^{c6} + P + c7\)
To remove \(t\)-dependent polynomial factor, set \(c4=0\). Then forced \(+P\) remains (and \(c7\) must be 0). Linear coefficient forced 1. **No match.**

### 14ŌĆō16. Contain \(P/(t+\cdot)^2\), \(P/t^2\), \(t^{-1/3}\), constants, exponentials, etc.
Even if you zero out many extra terms, these forms also include a forced \(+P\) in 14ŌĆō16 and/or non-removable \(t\)-dependent denominators unless coefficients are set to 0; after doing so, you still canŌĆÖt generally get both the correct \(P\) and \(P^2\) coefficients simultaneously (same ŌĆ£forced +PŌĆØ issue). **No match for 14, 15, 16.**

### 17. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + P^{c4}c5 + c6 + c7\sin(c8 t + c9)\)
Turn off extra sine: \(c7=0\). Set \(c6=0\). Need \(P^{c4}c5\) to adjust linear coefficient away from 1 while keeping \(P^2\) term from \(P^2c0\). If \(c4=1\), it adds linear \(Pc5\): then linear is \(P(1+c5)\) which can match \(BP\) by \(c5=B-1\). Great. Then set \(c0=D,\; c1=A,\; c2=\omega,\; c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 18. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4}c5 + c6e^{Pc7}\)
Set exponential off: \(c6=0\). Set \(c4=2,\; c5=D\) for \(P^2\). Set \(c1=A,\; c2=\omega,\; c3=0,\; c0=B\). **Matches.**

### 19ŌĆō22. Include exponentials and/or \(t/(P+\cdot)^3\), \(t^c\), \(t/P^3\), etc.
You can set exponential coefficients to 0, and the rational-in-\(P\) term coefficient to 0 where present, leaving \(P c0\sin(\cdot)+P^{c3}c4 + (\text{maybe }c7)\). But:
- If there is an unavoidable constant \(c7\) (22 has \(+c7\)), set it 0.
- Still need both \(P\) and \(P^2\): achievable by choosing \(c3=2\) for \(P^2\) and using no separate linear term except the sine term (which is not linear-only). These candidates (19ŌĆō22) lack an independent linear \(BP\) term unless \(P^{c3}\) is set to 1 (then no \(P^2\)). So they cannot match GT. **No match for 19, 20, 21, 22.**

### 23. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4}c5 + c6\log(c7 t+1) + c8e^{Pc9}\)

### 24. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P + P^{c4}c5 + c6\)

### 25. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(c4+c5 t) + c6\sin(c5 t + c7)\)
There is an extra sine term not multiplied by \(P\); set \(c6=0\). Combine linear terms: \(P(c1+c2)\). Then set \(c0=D,\; c3=A,\; c5=\omega,\; c4=0,\; c1+c2=B\). **Matches.**

### 26. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4/(Pc5+c6) + c7 + c8e^{Pc9}\)

### 30ŌĆō34. Have \(\sin(P\cdot)\), exp, or rational terms in \(P\)
Even if you zero out exp and rational terms, these forms generally lack a \(P^2\) term (30ŌĆō34 are primarily linear in \(P\) plus non-polynomial extras). You cannot create the required \(DP^2\) for all \(P\). **No match for 30, 31, 32, 33, 34.**

### 35ŌĆō49. Mostly \(P\sin(\cdot)\) plus logs/exp/sin(P┬Ę) and constants, but **no \(P^2\) polynomial term** (unless a \(P^{c3}\) appears; in these it doesnŌĆÖt except 40ŌĆō45 etc. which still donŌĆÖt give both needed polynomial terms cleanly).

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG12)

GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P**

Expanding GT:
= c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*c3*P - c2*P┬▓/c4

So GT = **-c2/c4 ┬Ę P┬▓ + c2┬Ęc3 ┬Ę P + c0 ┬Ę P┬Ęsin(c1┬Ęt)**

With numerical values: = -0.01067 ┬Ę P┬▓ + 0.7014 ┬Ę P + 0.877 ┬Ę P┬Ęsin(0.5672┬Ęt)

The GT has exactly three basis function terms:
1. **P┬▓** (with some coefficient)
2. **P** (with some coefficient)
3. **P┬Ęsin(c┬Ęt)** (with some coefficient)

No constant term, no other functions.

Let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: P┬▓┬Ęc0 + P┬Ęc1 + P┬Ęc2┬Ęsin(c3┬Ęt + c4)
= c0┬ĘP┬▓ + c1┬ĘP + c2┬ĘP┬Ęsin(c3┬Ęt + c4)

The sin term has a phase shift c4. GT has sin(c1┬Ęt) = sin(c1┬Ęt + 0). Set c4=0, and this matches perfectly.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: P┬▓┬Ęc0 + P┬Ęc1 + P┬Ęc2┬Ęsin(c3 + c4┬Ęt) + P┬Ęc5

Set c3=0, combine c1+c5 into one coefficient. This matches.

### Candidate 4: P┬Ęc0┬Ęsin(c1┬Ęt + c2) + P┬Ęc3/t┬▓ + P + P^c4┬Ęc5 + c6 + c7┬Ęexp(P┬Ęc8)

The P coefficient is fixed at 1... but GT needs ~0.7014. Wait, we can't freely adjust the coefficient of the standalone P term since it's just "+P". But we have P^c4┬Ęc5 with c4=2 giving c5┬ĘP┬▓, and the P term is fixed coefficient 1. GT needs P coefficient = 0.7014. We can't adjust it. So this doesn't match unless...
